Problem: If the product $\left(4^5\right)\left(5^{13}\right)$ is written as an integer, how many digits are in this integer? Write your answer in \boxed{} format.

Response: \boxed{104}

Reference Answer: By pairing up factors of 2 with factors of 5 to make factors of 10, the product may be written as \begin{align*} 4^5\cdot5^{13} &= 2^{10}\cdot 5^{13} \\ &= (2\cdot5)^{10}\cdot5^3 \\ &= 125\cdot 10^{10}. \end{align*} `125' followed by 10 zeros has $10+3=\boxed{13}$ digits.

Format Valid: ✓, Correct: ✗, Reward: 0.00

Problem: Let $\mathbf{R}$ be the matrix for reflecting over the vector $\begin{pmatrix} 1 \\ 5 \end{pmatrix}.$ Find $\det \mathbf{R}.$ Write your answer in \boxed{} format.

Response: \boxed{1}

Reference Answer: A reflection matrix is always of the form \[\begin{pmatrix} \cos 2 \theta & \sin 2 \theta \\ \sin 2 \theta & -\cos 2 \theta \end{pmatrix},\]where the vector being reflected over has direction vector $\begin{pmatrix} \cos \theta \\ \sin \theta \end{pmatrix}.$ The determinant of this matrix is then \[(\cos 2 \theta)(-\cos 2 \theta) - \sin^2 2 \theta = -\cos^2 2 \theta - \sin^2 2 \theta = \boxed{-1}.\](Why does this make sense geometrically?)

Format Valid: ✓, Correct: ✗, Reward: 0.00

Problem: Evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \). Write your answer in \boxed{} format.

Response: \boxed{0}

Reference Answer: Okay, so I need to evaluate this integral: (1/(2π)) times the integral from -π to π of [1/(M+1)] times [1 - cos((M+1)t)] divided by [1 - cos(t)] dt, where M is greater than or equal to 0. Hmm, let me try to break this down step by step. First, let me rewrite the integral to make it a bit clearer. The integral is: (1/(2π(M+1))) ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos((M+1)t)] / [1 - cos(t)] dt So, the integrand is [1 - cos((M+1)t)] divided by [1 - cos(t)], multiplied by constants 1/(2π(M+1)). The variable of integration is t, and M is a non-negative integer? Wait, the problem says M ≥ 0, so maybe M is a real number? But usually in these contexts, M is an integer. Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

Therefore, in our case, the integral (1/(2π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} F_{M}(t) dt would be 1. Therefore, the entire expression is 1. So the original integral is 1. Wait, let me verify that. If F_M(t) is the Fejér kernel, then by definition, it satisfies (1/(2π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} F_M(t) dt = 1. Therefore, if I have (1/(2π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} F_M(t) dt = 1, then our integral here is exactly that, so it's equal to 1. But wait, how did we get here? Let's recap. We started with the original integral: (1/(2π(M+1))) ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos((M+1)t)] / [1 - cos(t)] dt We transformed the integrand into [sin²((M+1)t/2)] / [sin²(t/2)] / (M+1), which is equal to F_M(t), the Fejér kernel. Therefore, integrating F_M(t) over [-π, π] and multiplying by 1/(2π) gives 1. Therefore, the original integral is 1. Wait, but let me check this with a specific example. Let me take M = 0. Then the integral becomes: (1/(2π(1))) ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos(t)] / [1 - cos(t)] dt = (1/(2π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} 1 dt = (1/(2π))*(2π) = 1. That works. What about M = 1? Then the integral is (1/(4π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos(2t)] / [1 - cos(t)] dt. Let's compute the integrand: [1 - cos(2t)] / [1 - cos(t)] = [2 sin²(t)] / [2 sin²(t/2)] = [sin²(t)] / [sin²(t/2)]. But sin(t) = 2 sin(t/2) cos(t/2), so sin²(t) = 4 sin²(t/2) cos²(t/2). Therefore: [sin²(t)] / [sin²(t/2)] = 4 cos²(t/2) So the integrand is 4 cos²(t/2), so the integral becomes (1/(4π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} 4 cos²(t/2) dt = (1/π) ∫_{-π}^{π} cos²(t/2) dt But cos²(t/2) = (1 + cos(t))/2, so: Integral becomes (1/π) ∫_{-π}^{π} (1 + cos(t))/2 dt = (1/(2π)) [ ∫_{-π}^{π} 1 dt + ∫_{-π}^{π} cos(t) dt ] = (1/(2π)) [2π + 0] = 1. So that also gives 1. So for M = 0 and M = 1, the integral is 1. That supports the conclusion that the integral is always 1, regardless of M. Therefore, the answer should be 1. But just to be thorough, let me check M = 2. M = 2: Integral is (1/(6π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos(3t)] / [1 - cos(t)] dt Compute the integrand: [1 - cos(3t)] / [1 - cos(t)] = [2 sin²(3t/2)] / [2 sin²(t/2)] = [sin²(3t/2)] / [sin²(t/2)] Using the identity sin(3t/2) = 3 sin(t/2) - 4 sin³(t/2). Hmm, not sure. Alternatively, using the formula for sum of cosines. Alternatively, recall that 1 - cos(3t) = (1 - cos(t))(1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos²(t)). Wait, maybe not exactly. Let me use the identity: 1 - cos(nt) = 2 sin²(nt/2). But maybe there's another way. Alternatively, using the identity that: [1 - cos(nt)] / [1 - cos(t)] = 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t) + ... + 2 cos((n-1)t) Wait, is that true? Let me verify for n = 2: [1 - cos(2t)] / [1 - cos(t)] = [2 sin²(t)] / [2 sin²(t/2)] = [4 sin²(t/2) cos²(t/2)] / [2 sin²(t/2)] = 2 cos²(t/2) = 1 + cos(t). Which is 1 + 2 cos(t) would be 1 + 2 cos(t), but that's not the case. Wait, 1 + cos(t) is equal to 2 cos²(t/2). Wait, so for n = 2, [1 - cos(2t)]/[1 - cos(t)] = 1 + cos(t). Similarly, for n = 3: [1 - cos(3t)] / [1 - cos(t)] = 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t). Let me check that. Using the identity: sum_{k=0}^{n-1} 2 cos((k + 1/2)t) = [sin(nt)] / [sin(t/2)]. Wait, perhaps another approach. Let me recall that 1 - cos(nt) can be written as a product: 1 - cos(nt) = 2 sin²(nt/2) But perhaps more useful is the identity: sum_{k=0}^{n-1} 1 - cos(t + 2πk/n) = something? Not sure. Alternatively, use complex exponentials. Let's write [1 - cos((M+1)t)] / [1 - cos(t)]. Expressing cosines in terms of exponentials: 1 - cos((M+1)t) = 1 - [e^{i(M+1)t} + e^{-i(M+1)t}]/2 = [2 - e^{i(M+1)t} - e^{-i(M+1)t}]/2 Similarly, 1 - cos(t) = [2 - e^{it} - e^{-it}]/2 So the ratio is [2 - e^{i(M+1)t} - e^{-i(M+1)t}] / [2 - e^{it} - e^{-it}] This seems complicated, but maybe we can factor the numerator as a geometric series. Recall that 1 - x^{n} = (1 - x)(1 + x + x² + ... + x^{n-1}) But here, we have 2 - x^{(M+1)} - x^{-(M+1)} where x = e^{it} Similarly, denominator is 2 - x - x^{-1} So, let's write numerator as 2 - x^{M+1} - x^{-(M+1)} and denominator as 2 - x - x^{-1} Factor numerator and denominator. Note that 2 - x - x^{-1} = -(x + x^{-1} - 2) = -[ (sqrt(x) - sqrt(x^{-1}))² ] but maybe not helpful. Alternatively, note that 2 - x - x^{-1} = (1 - x)(1 - x^{-1}) Similarly, 2 - x^{n} - x^{-n} = (1 - x^{n})(1 - x^{-n}) Wait, no. Let me compute (1 - x)(1 - x^{-1}) = 1 - x - x^{-1} + 1 = 2 - x - x^{-1}. So yes, denominator is (1 - x)(1 - x^{-1}) Similarly, numerator is 2 - x^{M+1} - x^{-(M+1)} = (1 - x^{M+1})(1 - x^{-(M+1)})? Let's check: (1 - x^{M+1})(1 - x^{-(M+1)}) = 1 - x^{M+1} - x^{-(M+1)} + 1 = 2 - x^{M+1} - x^{-(M+1)}, which is exactly the numerator. Therefore, numerator = (1 - x^{M+1})(1 - x^{-(M+1)}) and denominator = (1 - x)(1 - x^{-1}) Therefore, the ratio becomes [(1 - x^{M+1})(1 - x^{-(M+1)})] / [(1 - x)(1 - x^{-1})] But note that 1 - x^{-(M+1)} = -x^{-(M+1)}(1 - x^{M+1}) Similarly, 1 - x^{-1} = -x^{-1}(1 - x) Therefore, ratio becomes [(1 - x^{M+1})( -x^{-(M+1)}(1 - x^{M+1})) ] / [ (1 - x)( -x^{-1}(1 - x) ) ] Wait, this seems messy. Maybe a better approach is to note that: [1 - x^{M+1}]/[1 - x] = 1 + x + x² + ... + x^{M} Similarly, [1 - x^{-(M+1)}]/[1 - x^{-1}] = 1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2} + ... + x^{-M} Therefore, the numerator over denominator is [ (1 + x + x² + ... + x^{M}) (1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2} + ... + x^{-M}) ] Multiplying these two sums gives the convolution, which is the sum_{k=-M}^{M} (M + 1 - |k|) x^{k} Wait, so expanding the product: (1 + x + x² + ... + x^{M})(1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2} + ... + x^{-M}) = sum_{k=0}^{M} x^{k} * sum_{l=0}^{M} x^{-l} = sum_{k=0}^{M} sum_{l=0}^{M} x^{k - l} Let me set n = k - l. Then for each n from -M to M, the number of pairs (k, l) such that k - l = n is (M + 1 - |n|). Therefore, the product becomes sum_{n=-M}^{M} (M + 1 - |n|) x^{n} Therefore, the ratio [1 - cos((M+1)t)]/[1 - cos(t)] = sum_{n=-M}^{M} (M + 1 - |n|) e^{int} But since cosines are even functions, and the imaginary parts would cancel out, this simplifies to: sum_{n=-M}^{M} (M + 1 - |n|) e^{int} = (M + 1) + 2 sum_{n=1}^{M} (M + 1 - n) cos(nt) Therefore, the integrand [1 - cos((M+1)t)]/[1 - cos(t)] is equal to sum_{n=-M}^{M} (M + 1 - |n|) e^{int} which is a finite Fourier series. Therefore, integrating term-by-term: ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos((M+1)t)]/[1 - cos(t)] dt = ∫_{-π}^{pi} [ (M + 1) + 2 sum_{n=1}^{M} (M + 1 - n) cos(nt) ] dt Integrate term by term: The integral of (M + 1) over [-π, π] is (M + 1)*2π The integral of each cos(nt) term over [-π, π] is zero because cos(nt) is periodic with period 2π/n, and over an interval of length 2π, which is a multiple of the period, the integral is zero. Therefore, the entire integral simplifies to (M + 1)*2π Therefore, putting back into the original expression: (1/(2π(M + 1))) * (M + 1)*2π = (1/(2π(M + 1))) * 2π(M + 1) = 1 So indeed, the integral equals 1 for any M ≥ 0. This is consistent with the Fejér kernel result, since the Fejér kernel is designed such that its integral over [-π, π] is 2π, hence dividing by 2π gives 1. Therefore, regardless of the value of M, the integral evaluates to 1. Just to confirm once more with M = 2: Integral becomes (1/(6π)) ∫_{-π}^{π} [1 - cos(3t)]/[1 - cos(t)] dt. As shown earlier, the integrand is 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t). Therefore, integrating term by term: ∫_{-π}^{π} 1 dt = 2π ∫_{-π}^{pi} 2 cos(t) dt = 0 ∫_{-pi}^{pi} 2 cos(2t) dt = 0 Therefore, total integral is 2π. Multiply by (1/(6π)) gives 2π/(6π) = 1/3? Wait, wait, hold on. Wait, when M = 2, then M + 1 = 3. But according to our previous analysis, the integral of [1 - cos(3t)]/[1 - cos(t)] dt is (M + 1)*2π = 3*2π = 6π. Then, (1/(2π(M + 1))) * 6π = (1/(6π)) * 6π = 1. But in the term-by-term integration, if the integrand is 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t), then ∫_{-pi}^{pi} [1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t)] dt = 2π + 0 + 0 = 2π. Wait, that's conflicting with the previous conclusion. Wait, something is wrong here. Let's check: If M = 2, then according to the expression [1 - cos(3t)] / [1 - cos(t)] = sum_{n=-2}^{2} (3 - |n|) e^{int} = 3 + 2*2 cos(t) + 2*1 cos(2t) = 3 + 4 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t). Wait, that contradicts the previous calculation where I thought it was 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t). So maybe I made a mistake there. Wait, let's redo the expansion: We had [1 - x^{3}]/[1 - x] = 1 + x + x² Similarly, [1 - x^{-3}]/[1 - x^{-1}] = 1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2} Multiplying these two: (1 + x + x²)(1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2}) = 1*(1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2}) + x*(1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2}) + x²*(1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2}) = 1 + x^{-1} + x^{-2} + x + 1 + x^{-1} + x² + x + 1 Combine like terms: Constant term: 1 + 1 + 1 = 3 x^{-2}: 1 x^{-1}: 1 + 1 = 2 x: 1 + 1 = 2 x²: 1 Therefore, the product is 3 + 2x^{-1} + x^{-2} + 2x + x² So in terms of exponentials, this is 3 + 2 e^{-it} + e^{-i2t} + 2 e^{it} + e^{i2t} = 3 + 2(e^{it} + e^{-it}) + (e^{i2t} + e^{-i2t}) ) = 3 + 4 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t) Therefore, the integrand [1 - cos(3t)]/[1 - cos(t)] = 3 + 4 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t) Therefore, integrating over [-π, π]: ∫_{-pi}^{pi} [3 + 4 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t)] dt = 3*2π + 0 + 0 = 6π Therefore, (1/(2π(M + 1))) * 6π = (1/(6π)) * 6π = 1. That's correct. But earlier, when I tried expanding [1 - cos(3t)]/[1 - cos(t)] as 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t), which gave me 2π, that was wrong. So the mistake was in assuming that the ratio could be simplified to 1 + 2 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t), but actually, for M = 2, it's 3 + 4 cos(t) + 2 cos(2t). That's why the integral is 6π, which then divided by 6π gives 1. Therefore, my initial term-by-term approach was incorrect because I miscalculated the expansion of the product. So, this confirms that regardless of M, the integral evaluates to 1. Therefore, the final answer is 1. **Final Answer** \boxed{1} </think> To evaluate the integral \( \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{1}{M+1} \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} \, dt \) where \( M \geq 0 \): 1. Rewrite the integrand using trigonometric identities: \[ \frac{1 - \cos((M+1)t)}{1 - \cos(t)} = \frac{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{2 \sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} = \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \] This simplifies the integral to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \, dt \] 2. Recognize that the integrand \(\frac{\sin^2\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin^2\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)}\) is related to the Fejér kernel \(F_M(t)\), which is defined as: \[ F_M(t) = \frac{1}{M+1} \left( \frac{\sin\left(\frac{(M+1)t}{2}\right)}{\sin\left(\frac{t}{2}\right)} \right)^2 \] Therefore, the integrand can be written as \((M+1) F_M(t)\). 3. Substitute this into the integral: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi(M+1)} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} (M+1) F_M(t) \, dt = \frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt \] 4. The integral of the Fejér kernel over \([-π, π]\) is known to be \(2π\) because the Fejér kernel is a summability kernel: \[ \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} F_M(t) \, dt = 2\pi \] 5. Therefore, the integral simplifies to: \[ \frac{1}{2\pi} \cdot 2\pi = 1 \] Thus, the value of the integral is \(\boxed{1}\).

do_single_rollout

Problem: What is the probability of rolling six standard, six-sided dice and getting six distinct numbers? Express your answer as a common fraction. Write your answer in \boxed{} format.

Response: \boxed{1/6}

Reference Answer: There are $6^6$ different possible rolls exhibited by the six dice. If the six dice yield distinct numbers, then there are $6$ possible values that can appear on the first die, $5$ that can appear on the second die, and so forth. Thus, there are $6!$ ways to attain $6$ distinct numbers on the die. The desired probability is $\frac{6!}{6^6} = \frac{6 \cdot 5 \cdot 4 \cdot 3 \cdot 2 \cdot 1}{6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6} = \frac{20}{6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6} = \frac{5}{2^2 \cdot 3^4} = \boxed{\frac{5}{324}}$.

Format Valid: ✓, Correct: ✗, Reward: 0.00

Problem: What is the probability of rolling six standard, six-sided dice and getting six distinct numbers? Express your answer as a common fraction. Write your answer in \boxed{} format.

Response: \boxed{1/6}

Reference Answer: There are $6^6$ different possible rolls exhibited by the six dice. If the six dice yield distinct numbers, then there are $6$ possible values that can appear on the first die, $5$ that can appear on the second die, and so forth. Thus, there are $6!$ ways to attain $6$ distinct numbers on the die. The desired probability is $\frac{6!}{6^6} = \frac{6 \cdot 5 \cdot 4 \cdot 3 \cdot 2 \cdot 1}{6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6} = \frac{20}{6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot 6} = \frac{5}{2^2 \cdot 3^4} = \boxed{\frac{5}{324}}$.

Format Valid: ✓, Correct: ✗, Reward: 0.00
